Step 3 — Supabase schema

Bash: mkdir -p supabase

Write: supabase/schema.sql

-- Enable UUID extension
create extension if not exists "pgcrypto";

-- Table: posts
create table if not exists posts (
  id               uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
  title            text not null,
  slug             text unique not null,
  content          text not null default '',
  excerpt          text not null default '',
  category         text not null default 'industry'
                   check (category in ('ai-models','anthropic','industry','tools')),
  tags             text[] not null default '{}',
  cover_image_url  text not null default '',
  cover_image_prompt text not null default '',
  source_urls      text[] not null default '{}',
  status           text not null default 'draft'
                   check (status in ('published','draft')),
  auto_generated   boolean not null default false,
  created_at       timestamptz not null default now(),
  published_at     timestamptz
);

create index if not exists posts_status_published_at on posts (status, published_at desc);
create index if not exists posts_category on posts (category);
create index if not exists posts_slug on posts (slug);

-- Table: scout_memory
create table if not exists scout_memory (
  id           uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
  feed_url     text not null,
  item_guid    text not null,
  item_title   text not null default '',
  processed_at timestamptz not null default now(),
  post_id      uuid references posts(id) on delete set null,
  unique (feed_url, item_guid)
);

create index if not exists scout_memory_guid on scout_memory (feed_url, item_guid);

alter table posts enable row level security;
alter table scout_memory enable row level security;

create policy "Public read published posts"
  on posts for select
  using (status = 'published');

Step 4 — Lib files and API routes

import { createClient } from '@supabase/supabase-js'
const supabaseUrl = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL!
const supabaseAnonKey = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY!
const supabaseServiceKey = process.env.SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY!
export const supabase = createClient(supabaseUrl, supabaseAnonKey)
export const supabaseAdmin = createClient(supabaseUrl, supabaseServiceKey)

Write: lib/slugify.ts

export function slugify(text: string): string {
  return text
    .toLowerCase()
    .replace(/[^a-z0-9\s-]/g, '')
    .trim()
    .replace(/\s+/g, '-')
    .replace(/-+/g, '-')
    .slice(0, 80)
}

Write: lib/types.ts

export interface Post {
  id: string
  title: string
  slug: string
  content: string
  excerpt: string
  category: string
  tags: string[]
  cover_image_url: string
  cover_image_prompt: string
  source_urls: string[]
  status: 'published' | 'draft'
  auto_generated: boolean
  created_at: string
  published_at: string | null
}

Write: lib/createPost.ts

Shared post-creation logic used by both /api/posts/create and /api/posts/draft. Includes unique slug loop: queries Supabase, appends -2, -3 etc. until slug is unique. Sets published_at only when status is 'published'.

Write: app/api/health/route.ts

import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'
export async function GET() {
  return NextResponse.json({ status: 'ok' })
}

Write: app/api/posts/create/route.ts

POST endpoint. Checks x-api-key header against process.env.SCOUT_API_KEY. Validates: title (required), content (required), excerpt (required), category (must be one of ai-models/anthropic/industry/tools). Calls createPost(payload, 'published'). Returns:

{ success: true, post_id: "uuid", slug: "...", url: "https://aitrends.ng/post/..." }

Write: app/api/posts/draft/route.ts

Same as create but calls createPost(payload, 'draft'). Returns { success: true, post_id, slug }.

Static page. 5-step automation pipeline (Scout → Gemini → Pollinations → /api/posts/create → Slack), who it's for, FAIT attribution, "Read the latest digests →" CTA button.

Step 9 — SEO routes

Write: app/sitemap.ts

Dynamic sitemap. Queries Supabase for all published post slugs + published_at dates. Returns static routes (/, /about, 4 category pages) + one entry per post. Added export const dynamic = 'force-dynamic'.

Write: app/feed.xml/route.ts

RSS 2.0 feed. Queries latest 20 published posts. Returns application/xml with Cache-Control: public, max-age=3600. Each item includes title, link, guid, description (excerpt), pubDate, category, and cover image enclosure.

export default function robots() {

    sitemap: 'https://aitrends.ng/sitemap.xml',
  }
}

Second build attempt — FAILED

Bash: npm run build

✓ Compiled successfully in 1875ms
  Running TypeScript ...
  Finished TypeScript in 1681ms ...
  Collecting page data using 7 workers ...
Error: supabaseUrl is required.
    at <unknown> (.next/server/chunks/lib_supabase_ts_0li8sjd._.js:37:47256)
    ...
> Build error occurred
Error: Failed to collect page data for /sitemap.xml

Root cause: The original lib/supabase.ts called createClient() at module load time. During next build, Next.js tries to collect page data (statically render pages) with empty env vars — supabaseUrl is an empty string, which throws immediately.

Fix: Rewrote lib/supabase.ts using a lazy Proxy pattern. The Supabase client is only instantiated the first time a method is called on it — not at module import time. This allows the module to be imported safely at build time without env vars present.

Write: lib/supabase.ts (final version — lazy Proxy)

import { createClient, SupabaseClient } from '@supabase/supabase-js'

let _public: SupabaseClient | null = null
let _admin: SupabaseClient | null = null

function getPublic(): SupabaseClient {
  if (!_public) {
    const url = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL
    const key = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY
    if (!url || !key) throw new Error('Missing NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL or NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY')
    _public = createClient(url, key)
  }
  return _public
}

function getAdmin(): SupabaseClient {
  if (!_admin) {
    const url = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL
    const key = process.env.SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY
    if (!url || !key) throw new Error('Missing NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL or SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY')
    _admin = createClient(url, key)
  }
  return _admin
}

export const supabase = new Proxy({} as SupabaseClient, {
  get(_target, prop) {
    const client = getPublic()
    const value = (client as unknown as Record<string | symbol, unknown>)[prop]
    return typeof value === 'function' ? value.bind(client) : value
  },
})

export const supabaseAdmin = new Proxy({} as SupabaseClient, {
  get(_target, prop) {
    const client = getAdmin()
    const value = (client as unknown as Record<string | symbol, unknown>)[prop]
    return typeof value === 'function' ? value.bind(client) : value
  },
})

Also added export const dynamic = 'force-dynamic' to app/page.tsx, app/post/[slug]/page.tsx, app/category/[slug]/page.tsx, and app/sitemap.ts — this tells Next.js to render these at request time rather than attempting static generation at build time.

Provided step-by-step Supabase setup instructions:

  1. Go to app.supabase.com → sign up → New project → name: aitrends-ng → region: Europe West or US East → create
  2. SQL Editor → New query → paste supabase/schema.sql → Run → confirm "Success. No rows returned"
  3. Project Settings → API → copy three values: Project URL → NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL, anon key → NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY, service_role key → SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY
  4. Fill in .env.local with all values. Set SCOUT_API_KEY to any strong random string.
  5. Run npm run dev → visit http://localhost:3000 — homepage should return 200 with empty grid (no posts yet).

Warning issued: the service_role key bypasses RLS and has full DB access — never commit it to git, never expose in client-side code.

Still failing — even though the token belongs to FAIT-Blog. Checked token scopes via GitHub API:

Bash: curl -sI -H "Authorization: token ghp_●●●●●●●●●●●●[TOKEN-1-NO-SCOPES]" https://api.github.com/user | grep -i "x-oauth-scopes"

x-oauth-scopes:

Root cause: The token has no scopes — the x-oauth-scopes header is empty. A token with no scopes cannot read or write to any repository. It was generated without any permissions boxes ticked.

Bash: curl -s -H "Authorization: token ghp_●●●●●●●●●●●●[TOKEN-1-NO-SCOPES]" https://api.github.com/user | grep -E '"login"|"name"'

  "login": "FAIT-Blog",
  "name": "Fait",

Token belongs to the correct account. Only issue is the missing repo scope.

Instructed Felix to go to github.com/settings/tokens → generate new token (classic) → tick the top-level repo scope → generate → copy new token.

Check and tell what the issue is and how to fix this error: ## Error Type Runtime Error ## Error Message Event handlers cannot be passed to Client Component props. <article style={{...}} onMouseEnter=... onMouseLeave={function onMouseLeave} children=...> ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ If you need interactivity, consider converting part of this to a Client Component. at HeroPost (components/HeroPost.tsx:13:5) at HomePage (app/page.tsx:97:11)
Claude Code

Bash: head -1 components/HeroPost.tsx && head -1 components/PostCard.tsx

import Link from 'next/link'
import Link from 'next/link'

Root cause: Both HeroPost.tsx and PostCard.tsx use onMouseEnter / onMouseLeave event handlers but have no 'use client' directive. In the Next.js App Router, all components are Server Components by default. Server Components cannot handle browser events — event handlers only work in Client Components. The fix is 'use client' at the top of both files.

Note: PostCard.tsx has the same hover-lift handlers and would have thrown the identical error the moment a post card rendered.

Fetched all 10 visible posts and decoded their image prompts. Findings confirmed Felix's observation completely.

Root cause identified

The Scout Agent's Gemini prompt is extracting the RSS feed source as the entity (Hacker News, MIT Technology Review, TechCrunch, HuggingFace) rather than the actual subject of the story. Every image prompt resolves to a generic dark-background circuit illustration with a different publication logo — visually indistinguishable from post to post.

Evidence from decoded prompts:

Post titleWhat the image prompt actually usesWhat it should use
Beijing's Brain Chip Breakthrough: What It Means for African Devs"MIT Technology Review brand identity" + generic brain chipBeijing skyline + neural implant + African continent
African AI: Local Power, Global Scale, Agentic Future"HuggingFace logo"Africa map + AI nodes + local developers
Africa AI Digest: Google's Searchbox Shake-Up"TechCrunch AI logo"Google search interface + African cityscape
Stop Babysitting Your AI"Hacker News 'Y' logo"AI agent, broken code, developer frustration
I/O 2026: Your Essential Builder's Digest"Google AI logo" — only correct oneGoogle I/O stage + 2026 tech

Fix approach agreed

Two changes needed in the Scout Agent's Gemini prompt (not in the Next.js frontend):

  1. Entity extraction: Instruct Gemini to extract 3–5 visually concrete nouns from the story content itself — places, people, products, events — not the RSS source publication name. Example for "Beijing's Brain Chip Breakthrough": extract Beijing, brain chip, Africa, neural interface, breakthrough.
  2. Art style: Add a specific art direction style to every prompt — watercolour, ink sketch, vector flat, oil painting, digital illustration, etc. This forces visual variety between posts and makes each image feel crafted for that story. Felix's preferred styles: watercolour paint, vector, sketch/drawing. Style should vary per post or be chosen by Gemini to match the mood of the story.

Example of what the corrected prompt should produce for "Beijing's Brain Chip Breakthrough: What It Means for African Devs":

Watercolour-style illustration: a glowing neural implant chip floating above a
stylised Beijing skyline at night, connected by electric-blue data threads to an
outline of the African continent. Dark background, gold and blue accents,
painterly texture, no text in image.

This is entirely a Scout Agent change. Nothing in the Next.js frontend needs to change. Implementation deferred — Felix said "let's tackle these first" and indicated more points to come.

Felix

Claude Code

Read all source files: index.js, scout.js, feeds.js, gemini.js, memory.js, publisher.js, slack.js, image.js, .github/workflows/scout.yml, package.json, .env.

Also read /Users/felixokon/Documents/WEBSITE_AI_Generated_Xai/aitrends-project/aitrends.ng/app/api/posts/create/route.ts and aitrends.ng/.env.local to cross-check the API key setup.

What this project is

Scout Agent is an automated AI news digest pipeline for the AITrends.ng blog. Every 6 hours it: fetches the latest items from 10 RSS feeds (TechCrunch, VentureBeat, OpenAI, Google AI, HuggingFace, Hacker News, Simon Willison, DeepLearning.AI, Anthropic), deduplicates against a Supabase scout_memory table, groups fresh articles by category, sends each group to Gemini 2.5 Flash to generate a human-voice digest, builds a free cover image via Pollinations.ai, POSTs the digest to the AITrends.ng blog API, and fires a Slack notification to #aitrends-feed. Runs on GitHub Actions cron.

Problems found — in order of severity

1. Silent failures — the biggest issue

The GitHub Actions workflow had:

run: |
  timeout 110 node index.js || true

timeout 110 kills the process after 110 seconds. Fetching 10 RSS feeds + multiple Gemini calls + publishing + Slack can easily take 2–4 minutes. Scout may be dying mid-run every single time. || true means the workflow always reports green even when Scout crashed. No way to know if it's working.

2. index.js is wrong for GitHub Actions

index.js starts a node-cron daemon — fires runScout() once on startup, then schedules future runs every 6 hours. GitHub Actions already handles the scheduling and kills the process after timeout 110. The cron.schedule(...) line inside index.js will never fire. The workflow should run scout.js directly.

3. GitHub Actions secrets may not be set

The workflow references 7 secrets. If any haven't been added in GitHub → Settings → Secrets, every run fails with empty env vars — and || true hides it.

4. Wrong Supabase key name in workflow

memory.js uses process.env.SUPABASE_SECRET_KEY. The workflow also passed SUPABASE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY which nothing in the code uses — dead noise.

5. hasSeen() fails open on Supabase errors

In memory.js:24-29, if Supabase is down, hasSeen returns false — treating every article as new. A Supabase outage would cause Scout to re-publish every article it has ever seen as duplicate posts.

6. No validation before publishing

If Gemini returns a malformed response, the parser could produce empty content or title. Scout would call publishPost with an empty body and the blog API would reject it with 400.

7. No failure alerts

Slack notification only fires on success. If the entire run fails, you get nothing.

8. API key name mismatch (works, but fragile)

Scout's .env calls it BLOG_API_KEY. The blog's route.ts checks process.env.SCOUT_API_KEY. Different names, same value. If someone rotates one without the other it silently breaks.

Recommendations

  1. Rewrite the workflow to run runScout() directly, remove || true, add proper timeout and Slack failure alert
  2. Make hasSeen() throw on Supabase error instead of silently returning false
  3. Validate Gemini output before publishing
  4. Rename BLOG_API_KEY → SCOUT_API_KEY to match the blog API
Felix
Yes, let's fix everything if you can do so. But how will you verify to know these changes would work or is working?
Claude Code

Verification plan stated before touching any code:

  1. Fix all the code issues first
  2. Run node -e "import('./scout.js').then(m => m.runScout()).catch(...)" locally — the .env is present with real credentials, so this does a full real run against the actual Supabase, Gemini, and blog API
  3. Watch the console output step-by-step — logging is verbose enough to see exactly where it succeeds or fails
  4. If the local run completes cleanly, the GitHub Actions changes are verified by the same logic (GHA now does exactly what local run does)
  5. After pushing, trigger a workflow_dispatch manually from GitHub to watch the GHA logs

Fix 1 — .github/workflows/scout.yml

Edit: .github/workflows/scout.yml

Before:

jobs:
  run-scout:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest

    steps:
      ...
      - name: Run Scout
        env:
          SUPABASE_URL: ${{ secrets.SUPABASE_URL }}
          SUPABASE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY: ${{ secrets.SUPABASE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY }}
          SUPABASE_SECRET_KEY: ${{ secrets.SUPABASE_SECRET_KEY }}
          GEMINI_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.GEMINI_API_KEY }}
          BLOG_API_URL: ${{ secrets.BLOG_API_URL }}
          BLOG_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.BLOG_API_KEY }}
          SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL: ${{ secrets.SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL }}
        run: |
          timeout 110 node index.js || true

After:

jobs:
  run-scout:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    timeout-minutes: 8

    steps:
      ...
      - name: Run Scout
        env:
          SUPABASE_URL: ${{ secrets.SUPABASE_URL }}
          SUPABASE_SECRET_KEY: ${{ secrets.SUPABASE_SECRET_KEY }}
          GEMINI_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.GEMINI_API_KEY }}
          BLOG_API_URL: ${{ secrets.BLOG_API_URL }}
          SCOUT_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.SCOUT_API_KEY }}
          SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL: ${{ secrets.SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL }}
        run: node -e "import('./scout.js').then(m => m.runScout()).catch(e => { console.error(e); process.exit(1) })"

      - name: Notify Slack on failure
        if: failure()
        env:
          SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL: ${{ secrets.SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL }}
        run: |
          curl -s -X POST "$SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL" \
            -H 'Content-Type: application/json' \
            -d "{\"text\":\"❌ Scout Agent failed — check GitHub Actions: https://github.com/${{ github.repository }}/actions\"}"

Fix 2 — memory.js: hasSeen() throws instead of silently returning false

Edit: memory.js

Before:

  if (error) {
    console.error('memory.hasSeen error:', error.message)
    return false
  }

After:

  if (error) {
    throw new Error(`memory.hasSeen failed: ${error.message}`)
  }

Fix 3 — scout.js: validate Gemini output before publishing

Edit: scout.js

Before:

      // STEP 4 — Generate digest with Gemini
      console.log('  Generating digest with Gemini...')
      const digest = await generateDigest(capped, category)

      // STEP 5 — Build cover image URL

After:

      // STEP 4 — Generate digest with Gemini
      console.log('  Generating digest with Gemini...')
      const digest = await generateDigest(capped, category)

      if (!digest.title || !digest.content || digest.content.length < 100) {
        console.error(`  ❌ Gemini returned unusable content for ${category} — skipping`)
        continue
      }

      // STEP 5 — Build cover image URL

Local verification test of gemini-3.5-flash

Bash: node -e "import('./gemini.js').then(m => m.generateDigest([{title:'Test article...'}], 'industry'))..."

❌ Gemini API error: {
  "error": {
    "code": 503,
    "message": "This model is currently experiencing high demand. Spikes in demand are usually temporary. Please try again later.",
    "status": "UNAVAILABLE"
  }
}

503 = model ID valid. A 404 would mean "model not found." The 503 means "model exists but high demand right now." Still a risk for a production pipeline that runs every hour.

Genius fix: primary + fallback. Use gemini-3.5-flash as primary but automatically fall back to gemini-2.5-flash on 503. Best of both worlds — better quality when available, no disruption when overloaded.

Edit: gemini.js — add callGemini helper and fallback logic

Before (single URL constant + direct fetch):

const GEMINI_URL = '...gemini-2.5-flash:generateContent'

export async function generateDigest(articles, category) {
  ...
  const response = await fetch(`${GEMINI_URL}?key=...`, { ... })
  if (!response.ok) {
    const err = await response.text()
    throw new Error(`Gemini API error: ${err}`)
  }

After:

const GEMINI_PRIMARY   = '...gemini-3.5-flash:generateContent'
const GEMINI_FALLBACK  = '...gemini-2.5-flash:generateContent'

async function callGemini(url, body) {
  const response = await fetch(`${url}?key=${process.env.GEMINI_API_KEY}`, {
    method: 'POST',
    headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
    body: JSON.stringify(body)
  })
  return response
}

export async function generateDigest(articles, category) {
  ...
  const payload = {
    contents: [{ parts: [{ text: prompt }] }],
    generationConfig: { temperature: 0.7, maxOutputTokens: 4000 }
  }

  let response = await callGemini(GEMINI_PRIMARY, payload)

  if (response.status === 503) {
    console.log('  ⚠️  gemini-3.5-flash overloaded, falling back to gemini-2.5-flash...')
    response = await callGemini(GEMINI_FALLBACK, payload)
  }

  if (!response.ok) {
    const err = await response.text()
    throw new Error(`Gemini API error: ${err}`)
  }

const EVERGREEN_ENTITIES = [
  'anthropic', 'claude', 'openai', 'chatgpt', 'gpt-4', 'gpt-5', 'gpt',
  'google deepmind', 'gemini', 'microsoft', 'copilot', 'meta ai', 'llama',
  'nvidia', 'hugging face', 'mistral', 'groq', 'cohere', 'stability ai',
  'llm', 'large language model', 'foundation model', 'generative ai',
  'artificial general intelligence', 'agi', 'machine learning', 'neural network',
  'ai regulation', 'ai safety', 'ai agent', 'agentic', 'reasoning model',
  'claude code', 'github copilot', 'cursor', 'mcp', 'model context protocol',
  'transformer', 'diffusion model', 'multimodal'
]

function evergreenScore(article, vocab = EVERGREEN_ENTITIES) {
  const text = `${article.title} ${article.summary}`.toLowerCase()
  return vocab.filter(e => text.includes(e)).length
}

Articles sorted by score before slice(0, MAX_ARTICLES) — highest-value stories reach Gemini first.

Self-updating evergreen vocabulary — 3 parts built

Edit: memory.js — add loadEvergreens() and saveEvergreens()

export async function loadEvergreens() {
  const { data, error } = await supabase.from('evergreen_vocab').select('term')
  if (error) { console.error(...); return [] }
  return data.map(r => r.term)
}

export async function saveEvergreens(terms) {
  const rows = terms.map(t => t.trim().toLowerCase()).filter(t => t.length > 2).map(term => ({ term, source: 'auto' }))
  const { error } = await supabase.from('evergreen_vocab').upsert(rows, { onConflict: 'term', ignoreDuplicates: true })
  if (!error) console.log(`  📚 Saved ${rows.length} trending term(s) to evergreen vocab`)
}

Edit: gemini.js — add TRENDING_TERMS as 5th response label

TRENDING_TERMS: [comma-separated list of 3–5 specific entity names, technologies,
or companies central to this story that people will still search for in 2 years]

Parser updated to extract trendingTerms[]. Return value updated: { title, content, excerpt, imagePrompt, trendingTerms }

Edit: scout.js — load vocab at start, score with merged vocab, save after publish

const dbVocab = await loadEvergreens()
const allVocab = [...new Set([...EVERGREEN_ENTITIES, ...dbVocab])]
console.log(`  Vocabulary: ${EVERGREEN_ENTITIES.length} baseline + ${dbVocab.length} learned = ${allVocab.length} total terms`)

// After publish:
if (digest.trendingTerms?.length > 0) {
  console.log(`  Trending terms: ${digest.trendingTerms.join(', ')}`)
  await saveEvergreens(digest.trendingTerms)
}

Full system briefing delivered

What Scout is: A Node.js automation pipeline running on GitHub Actions every 6 hours. Fetches 10 RSS feeds → deduplicates against Supabase scout_memory → scores by evergreen vocabulary → groups by category → generates 800-word editorial digest via Gemini → builds cover image via Pollinations.ai → publishes to AITrends.ng API → saves trending terms to evergreen_vocab → sends Slack notification. Fully autonomous — Felix does nothing daily.

Current health:

MetricStatus
Cron schedule0 */6 * * * — running every 6h on GitHub Actions
Last successful runJune 3 00:14 UTC — 88 seconds
Posts published this run2 (industry + tools)
Evergreen vocab40 baseline + 5 learned terms
Gemini primary modelgemini-3.5-flash with gemini-2.5-flash fallback

Issue spotted in live run log: The TRENDING_TERMS being saved to Supabase are low-signal noise: microsoft assert, openclaw, micropython, stanford law school — not genuine AI entity names. The self-updating vocab feature is mechanically working but accumulating junk terms that pollute future evergreen scoring.

Skipped categories: anthropic and ai-models are both being skipped every run (only 1 fresh article each, below MIN_ARTICLES = 2). These categories need more RSS feeds added to feeds.js.

Felix
What do you recommend we do to enhance/ improve what has been done so far?
Claude Code

Full enhancement recommendations provided, organised into three tiers by impact and effort:

Tier 1 — Fix the gaps that hurt every run right now

1. Add more RSS feeds (feeds.js)

anthropic and ai-models categories are being skipped on most runs — only 1 fresh article each, below the MIN_ARTICLES = 2 threshold. That's wasted capacity every 6 hours. Missing feeds: Mistral blog, Cohere blog, Google DeepMind blog, Meta AI blog, Stability AI blog, Reddit r/MachineLearning, Reddit r/artificial. Easy change in feeds.js — no other files need to change.

2. Fix TRENDING_TERMS quality (gemini.js prompt)

The TRENDING_TERMS prompt instruction is too loose. Gemini returns noise: microsoft assert, openclaw, micropython, stanford law school. These pollute the evergreen vocabulary. The prompt needs a tighter constraint: "only proper nouns — company names, AI model names, researcher names, and established technology product names. No generic phrases, no verbs, no sentences." The self-updating vocab is a strong feature but only as good as the terms being saved.

3. OG meta tags on aitrends.ng (aitrends.ng project)

Every Slack notification links to a published post. That post has no social preview — no Open Graph title, description, or image. When shared on Twitter, LinkedIn, or WhatsApp, it renders as a blank link. This is a critical gap for content distribution. Fix is in the aitrends.ng Next.js project (dynamic generateMetadata() per post page). Not a scout-agent change.

Tier 2 — Medium effort, high long-term value

4. Email newsletter / audience capture

AITrends.ng has no way for a reader to subscribe. No email list means no return traffic. Scout is publishing 2–4 posts per day — but each post's audience is lost after the visit. A single-field email form connected to Buttondown or Beehiiv (both free) would start building a subscriber list. This is the highest ROI feature for long-term reach and entirely in the aitrends.ng project.

5. Phase 5 — Topic clustering

Instead of one digest per category, Scout finds the one story multiple sources are covering simultaneously and goes deep on it. Current posts are "here are 5 articles from this category" — useful but thin. A clustering step (group by shared keywords/entities before scoring) would produce fewer but significantly more authoritative posts. This is the biggest remaining architecture change in scout.js.

6. Google Search Console submission

The sitemap is already built (/sitemap.xml live on Vercel). It has not been submitted to Google Search Console. Every post Scout publishes is invisible to Google until this is done. This is a 10-minute task that unlocks all the SEO work already baked into the Gemini prompt (primary keywords, People Also Ask, semantic terms). Entirely manual — no code change needed.

Tier 3 — Infrastructure / longer-term

7. markSeen() retry logic

If Supabase hiccups after a post is published but before markSeen() completes, Scout will try to publish the same articles again on the next run. Not critical but will eventually cause a duplicate post. Add a 2-attempt retry with a 2s delay inside markSeen() in memory.js.

8. Admin dashboard on aitrends.ng

No way to see, delete, or manage what Scout has published without going into Supabase directly. A simple /admin/posts page (same pattern as the BFX site already built) would give visibility and control. The Supabase table already has all the data.

9. Render deployment for Scout

GitHub Actions cron is documented as unreliable on private repos — runs can be delayed or skipped entirely. The index.js daemon is already written for a persistent VPS. Render free tier would give a reliable always-on scheduler. Not urgent while GHA cron is running cleanly, but the risk of silent missed runs grows over time.

Top 3 to start

PriorityTaskWhy now
1Add more RSS feeds to feeds.jsFixes skipped-category problem immediately — more posts per run
2Tighten TRENDING_TERMS prompt in gemini.jsEvergreen vocab only works if the terms being saved are high-quality
3OG meta tags on aitrends.ngEvery Slack notification links to a post with no social preview

Core diagnosis: Prompt topic selection vs stated mission

Are the selected topics suitable for the Africa/Nigeria/West Africa AI mission?

CategoryTop article selectedScoreAfrica angle
industry"Publishers will be able to opt out of AI" (Google/publishers)[1]❌ None
ai-models"OpenAI public policy agenda"[1]❌ None
tools"Uber Caps Usage of AI Tools Like Claude"[9]❌ None — scored [9] only because "Claude" appears in the title

Root cause — not a prompt problem, a feeds problem:

All 10 RSS sources are 100% global/US-centric: TechCrunch, VentureBeat, MIT Tech Review, OpenAI, Google AI, HuggingFace, Hacker News, Simon Willison, DeepLearning.AI, Anthropic. No Africa content exists in the source material. No matter how the Gemini prompt is written, it cannot produce Africa-first journalism from sources that contain zero Africa content. Gemini is adding one Africa sentence per section — this is cosmetic Africa-washing, not genuine Africa reporting.

Does Scout go deep on headlines?

Scout takes up to 5 articles per category and asks Gemini to synthesise them. With global sources all reporting similar global things, the synthesis is coherent but shallow on Africa. A true deep-dive requires: (1) multiple sources covering the SAME Africa story, (2) Africa-specific RSS feeds to provide that material.

What suitable topics for the mission would look like:

  • "Nigeria's Central Bank issues first AI regulation for fintech" — from TechCabal
  • "Andela expands AI bootcamp to 5 West African cities" — from Techpoint.Africa
  • "Flutterwave integrates Claude API for fraud detection" — from Disrupt Africa
  • "MTN Nigeria deploys AI customer service across 50M subscribers" — from Stears

None of the current posts approach this. This is entirely fixed by adding Africa-specific RSS feeds to feeds.js.

Step 5 — Write merged SESSION_LOG.html

Bash: Python3 script executed to merge both session logs

Full Python script written and run:

import re

AITRENDS = '.../aitrends.ng/SESSION_LOG_AITRENDS.html'
SCOUT    = '.../scout-agent/SESSION_LOG_SCOUT.html'
OUT      = '.../aitrends-project/SESSION_LOG.html'

with open(AITRENDS, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    aitrends_raw = f.read()

with open(SCOUT, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    scout_raw = f.read()

# Extract body content from each file
def extract_body(html):
    m = re.search(r'<body>(.*)</body>', html, re.DOTALL)
    return m.group(1).strip() if m else html

aitrends_body = extract_body(aitrends_raw)
scout_body    = extract_body(scout_raw)

# Fix old paths → new paths in both bodies
def fix_paths(text):
    text = text.replace(
        '/Users/felixokon/Documents/WEBSITE_AI_Generated_Xai/aitrends.ng/',
        '/Users/felixokon/Documents/WEBSITE_AI_Generated_Xai/aitrends-project/aitrends.ng/'
    )
    text = text.replace(
        '/Users/felixokon/Documents/WEBSITE_AI_Generated_Xai/scout-agent: /',
        '/Users/felixokon/Documents/WEBSITE_AI_Generated_Xai/aitrends-project/scout-agent/'
    )
    text = text.replace(
        '/Users/felixokon/Documents/WEBSITE_AI_Generated_Xai/scout-agent/',
        '/Users/felixokon/Documents/WEBSITE_AI_Generated_Xai/aitrends-project/scout-agent/'
    )
    return text

aitrends_body = fix_paths(aitrends_body)
scout_body    = fix_paths(scout_body)

# Build merged HTML with Part 1 / Part 2 dividers, shared CSS, single <html> wrapper
merged = f"""<!DOCTYPE html>...
Part 1 — aitrends.ng (Blog Frontend)
{aitrends_body}
Part 2 — scout-agent (Automation Pipeline)
{scout_body}
..."""

with open(OUT, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    f.write(merged)

print(f"Written: {OUT}")
print(f"Total lines: {len(merged.splitlines())}")

Bash: curl -s "https://image.pollinations.ai/prompt/Lagos%20developer?seed=12345&width=200&height=200&nologo=true"

{"x402Version":1,"error":"Queue full for IP: 2a06:98c0:3600::103: 1 requests already queued (max: 1). Get unlimited access at https://enter.pollinations.ai","accepts":[{"scheme":"exact","network":"base","maxAmountRequired":"1000","resource":"https://image.myceli.ai/...","description":"Pollinations legacy image — pay to bypass rate limit","mimeType":"image/jpeg","payTo":"0xDAFc006c05Ea6BF5D19cA1D5ffB70f4Cdfb40409","asset":"0x833589fCD6eDb6E08f4c7C32D4f71b54bdA02913"}]}

Root cause — two bugs introduced in Round 1

Bug 1 — model=flux in image.js

Added in Round 1 believing Flux Schnell was faster and free. It is NOT free — Pollinations returns HTTP 402 Payment Required for any URL containing model=flux. Every new post image published after Round 1 was broken.

Bug 2 — unoptimized on next/image grid cards

With unoptimized, the browser fetches Pollinations URLs directly instead of going through Vercel's optimizer. A page with 9 cards fires 9 concurrent image requests. Pollinations free tier allows only 1 concurrent request per IP — so 8 of 9 cards get HTTP 402 rate-limited and never load.

Immediate fix applied

Edit: scout-agent/image.js — remove model=flux

Before: return \`https://image.pollinations.ai/prompt/\${encoded}?seed=\${seed}&width=1200&height=630&nologo=true&model=flux\`

After: return \`https://image.pollinations.ai/prompt/\${encoded}?seed=\${seed}&width=1200&height=630&nologo=true\`

Comment updated: "No model parameter — Pollinations free tier does not support model selection. model=flux returns HTTP 402 Payment Required."

Edit: PostCard.tsx — replace next/image with plain img tag

Before: <Image src=... fill unoptimized style={{objectFit: 'cover'}} />

After: Plain <img> tag with gradient background always shown, image loads on top. loading="lazy" staggers requests. onError hides the img silently if Pollinations fails — gradient stays visible.

Edit: HeroPost.tsx — same approach as PostCard

Replaced <Image fill priority unoptimized> with plain <img> + onError handler. Gradient background always present as fallback.

Bash: npm run build

✓ Compiled successfully. TypeScript clean. All routes correct.

Critical finding: Pollinations is returning 402 from GitHub Actions server IP too. Not a rate limit issue — Pollinations has adopted the x402 standard (HTTP 402 micro-payment protocol). All image generation now requires crypto payment in USDC on Base blockchain. Pollinations is effectively no longer free. The error message includes "x402Version":1 — this is a deliberate API change on their side.

Felix
While you think of polination ai alternatives (free) for this project, can you program it such that our image generation (based on our prompts) get queued till the image ready (completed generation) and ushered to cloud storage of our choosing, the post get lauched by taking the image from the cloud storage. Nothing get published untill everything (maybe image(s)) is ready. So we don't get forced to publish in a very short time frame at the count of our 6-hourly intervals. Our 6-hourly countdown trigger the action, but the completing of all generated post does not necessarily get published within that hour but can be several hour later it doesn't matter so long it delivered/ executed a perfectly planned post/ job. Please spent time to digest this an let me know you understand me.
Claude Code

Confirmed understanding exactly. Reflected back the two-phase architecture:

  • Phase 1 (every 6h cron): RSS fetch → score → Gemini digest → submit image job → save to pending_posts table → EXIT. Nothing published.
  • Phase 2 (separate, polling): Check image status → if ready, download → upload to cloud storage → call /api/posts/create → update status → Slack.
  • Nothing published until image is permanently in cloud storage.

Identified three free image providers to evaluate:

  • Hugging Face Inference API — free $0.10/month renewing, FLUX Schnell, synchronous (Phase 2 generates)
  • Fal.ai — $0.003/image, FLUX Schnell, native async queue (Phase 1 submits, Phase 2 polls)
  • AI Horde — crowdsourced, free forever, SDXL quality, async queue
Felix
We have upgraded our processes and we need to know it's working with the barest minimum (free). I love the sound of fal.ai, but let's stick to our policy and go for Hugging Face and later upgrade to fal.ai. Can you set it up such that both Hugging Face and Fal.ai are fused into the system so that we just have to enter the appropriate credentials and activate either of the service.
Claude Code

WebFetch: huggingface.co/docs/api-inference/pricing

Confirmed: Hugging Face gives every free account $0.10/month in credits that restore on the 1st of every month. No signup fee. FLUX Schnell at ~$0.001/image = ~100 images/month free.

WebFetch: fal.ai/pricing

Confirmed: Fal.ai is pure pay-as-you-go, credit-based. Credits do not restore monthly. FLUX Schnell: $0.003/image. At 4 posts/day: ~$0.36/month. No confirmed free signup credits on the current pricing page.

AI Horde comparison provided: free forever, async queue (true async fits Phase 1/Phase 2), SDXL quality (not FLUX), variable wait times 30s–20min+. Added as third option.

Recommended: use all three as provider options behind one IMAGE_PROVIDER env var. Start with HF, upgrade to Fal, fall back to AI Horde if needed.

Polling cycle: recommended 5 minutes (HF generates in ~10–60s, Fal.ai in 2–5s — 30-min polling was too conservative).

Write: image-providers/huggingface.js (101 lines)

HF Inference API, FLUX.1-schnell via router.huggingface.co. Synchronous — submitJob() returns { jobId: null } immediately (no job to submit). processJob() calls HF, waits up to 90s, returns image buffer. Handles 503 (model loading) and 429 (rate limit) as { done: false } — retries next cycle. X-Wait-For-Model: true header avoids cold-start 503.

Write: image-providers/fal.js (111 lines)

Fal.ai async queue. submitJob() POSTs to queue.fal.run/fal-ai/flux/schnell, returns request_id immediately. processJob() checks /requests/{id}/status — returns { done: false } if IN_QUEUE/IN_PROGRESS, downloads image when COMPLETED, throws on FAILED.

Write: image-providers/aihorde.js (147 lines)

AI Horde crowdsourced GPU network. submitJob() POSTs to stablehorde.net/api/v2/generate/async, returns task UUID. processJob() polls /generate/check/{id} — returns { done: false } if done: false, fetches result from /generate/status/{id} when done. Handles R2 CDN URL and base64 image formats. Model: AlbedoBase XL (SDXL). Note: free forever but not FLUX quality.

Write: image-providers/index.js (76 lines)

Unified interface. Reads IMAGE_PROVIDER env var (huggingface default). submitImageJob(prompt) delegates to active provider's submitJob(). processImageJob(jobId, prompt, provider) accepts the provider stored in pending_posts record — ensures existing pending posts still complete via their original provider even if IMAGE_PROVIDER is changed mid-flight.

Write: complete.js (142 lines)

Phase 2 worker. Flow:

  1. Call getPendingPosts() — also resets posts stuck in 'generating' >15 min
  2. For each post: set status = 'generating' (prevents concurrent runs picking same post)
  3. Call processImageJob(jobId, prompt, provider)
  4. If not done: reset to 'pending_image', continue (retry next 5-min cycle)
  5. If done: upload buffer to Supabase Storage → call publishPost() → update status 'published' → notifySlack()
  6. On error: reset to 'pending_image' unless MAX_ATTEMPTS (8) exceeded → mark 'failed'

Write: .github/workflows/complete.yml (54 lines)

New GHA workflow. Cron: */5 * * * * (every 5 minutes). timeout-minutes: 10. Env: SUPABASE_URL, SUPABASE_SECRET_KEY, BLOG_API_URL, SCOUT_API_KEY, SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL, IMAGE_PROVIDER, HF_API_TOKEN, FAL_API_KEY, AIHORDE_API_KEY. Failure step sends Slack alert.

Fix 1 — One story per post (gemini.js line 51)

Edit: gemini.js — CONTENT RULES section

Before:

- Give each article its own <h3> section

After:

- ONE STORY ONLY. From the articles provided, identify the SINGLE most important
  and Africa-relevant story. Write your entire piece about that one story. If other
  articles provide supporting evidence for the same theme, weave them in. If they
  cover different topics entirely, ignore them.
- Use <h3> headings to explore different ANGLES of your chosen story (technical
  depth, cost impact, Africa opportunity, regulatory risk, historical precedent)
  — NOT one <h3> per source article. Never write a roundup of unrelated stories.

Also updated TITLE and CONTENT response labels: "ONE topic only, not a roundup" and "ONE story with h3 headings for different angles".

Fix 2 — Break the repetitive image pattern (gemini.js lines 68–88)

Python script: replace image prompt rules section (lines 67–87)

Complete replacement of the RULES FOR IMAGE PROMPT and examples. Key changes:

  • BANNED COMPOSITIONS list added — explicitly forbidden: person at laptop, developer near window, city skyline as backdrop, "young African professional + laptop + Lagos cityscape" combination
  • Scene diversity encouraged — financial flows, products depicted directly, event scenes (handshakes/launches/protests), maps & geography, infrastructure (data centres/towers/cables), abstract conceptual art
  • 4th art style added — bold risograph print (high contrast, two dominant colours)
  • Style rotation rule — no same art style in consecutive posts
  • Single GOOD example replaced with 3 diverse examples:
    1. Funding story: naira symbol transforming into digital data streams rising to cloud nodes
    2. Regulation story: scales-of-justice with human/robotic hands, Nigerian flag colours
    3. Model release: brain made of hexagonal cells labelled with African city names
  • BAD example updated to the specific pattern we're prohibiting

Root cause of 429: The regeneration step fired immediately after Phase 1 (scout.js) completed. Phase 1 had just run (queuing 4 new posts), and the GHA runner IP was rate-limited by HF from those previous API interactions. All requests failed instantly with HTTP 429 Too Many Requests.

Fix: regenerate-images.js (v2 — queue-based approach)

Insight: Instead of calling HF directly (which rate-limits when many requests fire together), insert all posts that need images into pending_posts table. Phase 2 (complete.yml) already handles HF calls one at a time every 5 minutes. No rate limit issues. Spreads 28 image generations across ~140 minutes automatically.

Write: regenerate-images.js (complete rewrite — 100 lines)

New approach:

  1. Query all published posts with Pollinations URLs and stored cover_image_prompt
  2. For each, INSERT into pending_posts with post_id set to the existing post's ID
  3. Phase 2 picks them up every 5 minutes, generates HF image, uploads to Storage, updates the post
  4. Skip posts already queued or already having Supabase Storage URLs

Edit: complete.js — add "update existing post" path

Before: complete.js always called publishPost() to create a new post via /api/posts/create.

After: if post.post_id is set in the pending_posts record, it means this is an image regeneration for an existing post. Instead of creating a new post, directly updates cover_image_url on the existing post in Supabase:

if (post.post_id) {
  // Update existing post's image — don't create a new one
  await supabase.from('posts')
    .update({ cover_image_url: publicUrl })
    .eq('id', post.post_id)
} else {
  // New post — publish via /api/posts/create as usual
  publishResult = await publishPost({ ... })
}

Phase 1 failure log (gh run view 27032868650 --log)

Content generation succeeded: "Why Safaricom's $6 Plan..." queued as id:37. The failure was in the "Trigger Phase 2" step:

HTTP 403: Resource not accessible by integration
(https://api.github.com/repos/FAIT-Blog/scout-agent/actions/workflows/complete.yml)

Root cause: GITHUB_TOKEN on schedule-triggered runs cannot dispatch workflow_dispatch on other workflows, even with permissions: actions: write in the YAML. GitHub restricts this to prevent infinite loops on scheduled runs. The fix from Session #4 (adae741) works for workflow_dispatch-triggered runs only — not for schedule-triggered runs, which is when the 403 recurs.

Impact: Phase 1 correctly marks itself as "failed" → GHA scheduler becomes unreliable for Phase 1's own cron. The content was queued but Phase 1 ran as "failed" every time it ran on schedule.

Fix 2 — complete.js: Fix Slack notification URL (UUID → slug)

In the image-regeneration branch (~line 105), the Slack notification URL was built as /post/${post.post_id} where post.post_id is a UUID. Since all 28 existing posts went through regeneration in Session #3, every Slack notification sent during that batch had a UUID URL that 404s. Fixed by querying the post's slug from Supabase after the image update:

// After .update() call succeeds:
const { data: existingPost } = await supabase
  .from('posts')
  .select('slug')
  .eq('id', post.post_id)
  .single()
const postSlug = existingPost?.slug || post.post_id
const siteUrl = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SITE_URL || 'https://aitrends-ng.vercel.app'
publishResult = {
  post_id: post.post_id,
  url: `${siteUrl}/post/${postSlug}`,
}

supabase was already imported at the top of complete.js — no new import needed.

Edit: scout-agent/complete.js — image-update branch (~line 105)

Fix 3 — scout.yml: Remove broken "Trigger Phase 2" step

The gh workflow run complete.yml step fails with HTTP 403 whenever Phase 1 runs on schedule (not workflow_dispatch). This is a GitHub limitation: GITHUB_TOKEN on scheduled runs cannot dispatch workflow_dispatch events, regardless of the permissions: actions: write declaration. Since cron-job.org is already reliably triggering Phase 2 every 30 minutes (confirmed success in all 18 runs checked), the internal trigger is redundant. Removing it eliminates the false failure that was making Phase 1 appear to fail and causing GHA to skip its scheduled runs.

Also removed permissions: actions: write since nothing in the workflow needs it anymore.

The news about AI and DeepFake and fake news in Nigeria were examples of how a news is supposed to be written. A news carries a headline, and all the body... all the content of that story is talking about the headline. It stays with the headline. And when the person was done exhausting his points, she ends the conversation there. But our own news — every single post carries a heading and then starts carrying subheadings of different subject matters or different news entirely. So it becomes like five to six news under one heading inside one page, and carries an image that does not correlate with all the news that are in that single page. I have two issues about the way our posts show up. The example I gave about the AI deepfakes — the minister that spoke, the face of that minister is shown. And so it makes it look: okay, this is the minister that is speaking and showing his concern about AI and lying. While I said that, I said I also want you to take note that the image agrees with the message. The message is telling us who says it, and the picture of the person is showing to indicate that that's the person that is saying it. In our own case, the pictures or the images do not correlate with the message, and the image looks funny. So don't rush to alter things and assure me that all will be well. Honest assessment — no code touched

Problem 1 — Multi-topic posts: The prompt says "ONE STORY ONLY" but Gemini receives 5 articles from 5 different sources about 5 different things and writes one heading with 4–5 <h3> sections each covering a different article. The instruction exists but the input defeats it. You cannot write one coherent story when the raw material is 5 unrelated stories.

Problem 2 — Wrong images: Real news images are photographs — the minister's face, the building, the product, the event. We are generating abstract AI art through HuggingFace FLUX. No AI image generator can produce a photograph of a real Nigerian minister. The gap between what real journalism looks like and what our system produces is fundamental, not a prompt wording issue.

These two problems require different thinking, not just prompt edits. No code was touched.

Template provided for Felix to fill in

A structured specification template was given covering 5 sections:

  • Section 1 — News Sources: Felix lists specific websites with (NIGERIA)/(AFRICA)/(GLOBAL) tags
  • Section 2 — Post Structure: Number of topics, structure format (news-style vs feature), direct quotes, word count, tone
  • Section 3 — Images: Source article photo vs AI illustration, fallback behaviour, Felix's own description of what a good news image looks like
  • Section 4 — One Example Post: Felix writes or pastes one perfect post (headline + body + image description) — the most valuable input possible
  • Section 5 — What to Reject: Story types that must never appear on AITrends.ng

Instruction to Felix: fill in all sections and return. No code will be written until the template is returned and any clarifying questions are resolved.

Key insight noted

Felix observed: "I can see that you easily take an illustration as an example and context literally." This is accurate. When the Gemini prompt contained example image descriptions (e.g. "For a funding story: Watercolour painting of naira flowing upward…"), Gemini followed the example type literally on every post rather than understanding the underlying principle. Examples in AI prompts are treated as patterns to repeat, not principles to understand. The solution is not better examples — it is a different approach to images entirely (fetching from source vs generating).

Claude Code

Investigation — confirmed root cause

Explore agent: read gemini.js lines 19-21, fetcher.js, scout.js data flow

What Gemini currently receives per article:

TITLE: AI Deepfakes Threaten Nigeria's Security, Group Warns
SOURCE: Premium Times Nigeria
SUMMARY: The Grassroots Mobilisation Initiative warned... [100-300 chars]

That's all. 100-300 characters of RSS summary. Then the prompt demands 800+ words with named people, direct quotes, specific African facts, and four detailed sections. Gemini has no real content to draw from, so it fabricates to fill the gap. This is not misbehaviour — it is a predictable response to impossible constraints given no source material.

What already exists but was never used for RSS articles: fetcher.js has fetchContent() — extracts up to 4,000 characters of real article body from any URL, with HTML stripping, semantic container detection, 10-second timeout, error handling. It is only called for Felix's manual #scout-editor inputs. It has never been called for regular RSS articles.

Model switching decision

Asked Felix: keep Gemini (with fixes) OR switch to Perplexity Sonar Pro (real-time internet search) OR fix source material first.

Felix chose: Part 1 only for now — fix source material, assess quality before deciding on model switch.

Fix implemented (commit 3fd9671)

Edit: scout.js

  • Added import { fetchContent } from './fetcher.js'
  • Before calling generateDigest(), loop over capped articles and call fetchContent(article.link)
  • Attach result as article.fullText
  • Log character count per article

Edit: gemini.js

  • Expanded articleList to include FULL TEXT field (4000 chars) alongside TITLE, SOURCE, URL, SUMMARY
  • Added SOURCE RULES block: write only from provided FULL TEXT; no invented facts; no fabricated quotes; attribute with "according to [Source]"; if source is thin, write conservatively not inventively

Claude Code — diagnosis

Black images — root cause found

# Download cover 62 (jimp-styled) and sample pixels
node → Jimp.read('/tmp/test_cover.jpg')
  (0,0)    → rgb(1,2,10)
  (600,315) → rgb(1,2,10)
  (1199,629) → rgb(1,2,10)
  (300,150) → rgb(1,2,10)
  (900,450) → rgb(1,2,10)

Every pixel is rgb(1,2,10) — near-black. The jimp composite() was applying the overlay (#0a0a2a47) and multiplying the background contribution by zero (JPEG pixels loaded without alpha channel, treated as fully transparent by jimp's blend engine). Result: overlay×0.28 + background×0 = near-black solid colour. All 7 recent jimp-styled covers are valid JPEGs at 21KB but pure black.

Asterisks — root cause

Post body stored with markdown **bold** syntax. Post page uses dangerouslySetInnerHTML — raw HTML render. Markdown bold is not HTML; asterisks display literally.

jimp import removed. styleWithAI() function deleted. When source photo found: use it directly, no transformation.

Removed: 800-word minimum, 4-section structure, SEO rules, synthesis requirements, editorial stance, Africa-first mandate expansion. Kept: Africa Relevance GATE, no-markdown rule.

2. AI signal gate built — hasAISignal() — commit 000c25f

Root cause: Nigerian general news feeds (Premium Times, BusinessDay, Eagle Online) were sending sports, crime, and fintech stories into the pipeline. The Africa GATE only rejected categories with no African angle — it did not check whether the article was about AI at all.

Fix: hasAISignal() added to scout.js. Checks article title and fetched body against an explicit AI keyword list. Articles scoring 0 on both checks are dropped before Gemini scoring. This is an implicit filter (no Gemini call) — fast and free.

// scout.js — hasAISignal() (commit 000c25f)
const AI_SIGNAL_TERMS = [
  'ai', 'artificial intelligence', 'machine learning', 'deep learning',
  'neural', 'llm', 'large language model', 'generative', 'chatbot',
  'automation', 'algorithm', 'nlp', 'computer vision', 'robotics',
  'openai', 'anthropic', 'google ai', 'gemini', 'claude', 'gpt',
  'huggingface', 'mistral', 'model', 'training data', 'inference'
];

function hasAISignal(article) {
  const text = ((article.title || '') + ' ' + (article.fullText || '')).toLowerCase();
  return AI_SIGNAL_TERMS.some(term => text.includes(term));
}

// Applied in runScout() before evergreenScore():
const aiFiltered = deduped.filter(a => hasAISignal(a));
console.log(`🤖 AI signal filter: ${deduped.length} → ${aiFiltered.length} articles`);

3. BusinessDay Nigeria sports feed identified

The South Africa football post (about AI in FIFA World Cup stadium management) was traced to BusinessDay Nigeria's RSS feed. The feed contains general business and sports news, not AI-specific content. The AI signal gate would correctly drop a pure sports headline, but "AI in World Cup stadiums" passes the gate (contains "AI"). Felix's note: keep the gate, monitor whether BusinessDay content improves or needs removal.

Felix — concept for search-aggregate pipeline
Using "MTN Enlists Alipay's Parent Company, Ant International, to Revitalize MoMo Mobile Money in Nigeria" as an example, the key word I picked and searched on the internet browser was "MTN and Alipay news" and it gave me the same news as a result. So I was wondering what method can we use so that when we get a news that fits our criteria for AI relevance, the exact same news is searched and fished from the search engine results and the bot will pick minimum of just 3 (three) of that same news, though may have varying headlines and blend them into our own one single same news and publish. One of the instructions is that the bot will have to read fully any of the results to know for sure that the news is the SAME before it will add to bucketlist and then blend them beautifully for a unique post. We can be adding news blog/sites that frequently carry the same news relevant to our preference. In that case if our word count reaches 800 or more fine, if not we settle with the fact that we have a unique post/news that is current and evergreen.
Claude Code — confirmed understanding, proposed architecture

Confirmed understanding. Architecture proposed:

  1. RSS finds article → extract search query from title
  2. Web search that query (Tavily API)
  3. Fetch full text of each result, verify same story (2+ named entity overlap)
  4. Build bucket list — minimum 3 verified same-story sources
  5. Gemini blends all 3+ into one unique Africa-first post
  6. Self-learning: domains appearing 5+ times in bucket list → promoted to priority sources (checked first in future searches)

Felix added: reverse demotion — priority sources silent for 7 days get dropped; can re-earn priority from scratch.

Felix — screenshot of Google search results for "MTN and Alipay news"
[Screenshot attached — Google results showing Bloomberg, Business Insider Africa, Techmoonshot, Tech Labari, Moneycentral Nigeria, Afridigest, The Whistler all covering the same MTN/Alipay story] For curated list of sites, I meant that from the search results just as shown, the bot should take note of which website often fall into the bucket list for showing/featuring the same news headline regularly for at least five (5) consecutive times, then those sites can be qualified to be considered and curated as priority list. Same apply in reverse to those sites that have no news on topics that befits our website/project should be dropped after seven (7) days and can be picked back if they meet the criteria following the afore mentioned process. Build it
Claude Code — built search-aggregate pipeline (commit 47a0c8c)

Files created / modified

search.js (new)

  • buildSearchQuery(title) — strips stop words + possessives, keeps named entities, max 8 words
  • searchSameStory(title, prioritySources) — Tavily POST, search_depth: advanced, include_raw_content: true, max 8 results. Priority sources sorted to front of results.

verify.js (new)

  • extractEntities(text) — regex extracts Title Case sequences (1–4 words), filters 60-word stop list
  • isSameStory(original, candidate) — compares FULL BODY text (not just headline). 2+ shared named entities = same story. Rejects keyword-adjacent stories.
  • extractDomain(url) — returns bare hostname without www.

memory.js (3 new functions)

trackSourceReputation(domains[])
  → upsert: increment count + update last_seen
  → if count >= 5 and not already priority: set is_priority=true, log promotion

getPrioritySources()
  → SELECT domain WHERE is_priority=true
  → returned to scout.js, passed to searchSameStory()

dropStaleSourceReputations()
  → SELECT priority sources WHERE last_seen < now - 7 days
  → SET is_priority=false, count=0, dropped_at=now()
  → logs each demotion

gemini.js — generateBlendedDigest() (new function)

  • Receives bucketList[] of {title, url, content} from verified search results
  • Prompt: "You are given N sources covering the same story. Blend them into one unique original post."
  • Same Africa GATE, same SKIP mechanism, same output format as generateDigest()
  • Word count: whatever sources naturally support — no minimum, no padding
  • Same retry logic (3 attempts, 12s delay, primary→fallback)

scout.js — pipeline updated

  • Imports: searchSameStory, isSameStory, extractDomain, trackSourceReputation, getPrioritySources, dropStaleSourceReputations, generateBlendedDigest
  • Step 0: dropStaleSourceReputations() + getPrioritySources() added before RSS fetch
  • After RSS scoring: searchSameStory(topArticle.title, prioritySources)
  • Verification loop: isSameStory() for each result → builds bucketList
  • If bucketList.length >= 3: blend mode → generateBlendedDigest()
  • If bucketList.length < 3: single-source fallback → generateDigest() (unchanged)
  • trackSourceReputation() called for all bucket domains
  • sourceUrls: all bucket URLs in blend mode (up to 5), single URL in fallback
  • Post tagged 'blended' in blend mode, 'digest' in fallback

Supabase table SQL

supabase/add-source-reputation.sql
CREATE TABLE source_reputation (
  id           bigint generated always as identity primary key,
  domain       text unique not null,
  count        integer default 0,
  last_seen    timestamptz,
  is_priority  boolean default false,
  promoted_at  timestamptz,
  dropped_at   timestamptz,
  created_at   timestamptz default now()
)

Felix — editorial channel optimisation question
There is an optional channel to provide source materials by the editorial through Slack can you help me look at what can be optimised.
Claude Code — audit of felix.js, 5 optimisation opportunities identified

Read felix.js in full (126 lines). The current design works but has five structural problems:

  1. Two Slack API calls per run regardless of whether Felix has posted anything. conversations.list paginates to find the channel ID, then conversations.history fetches the last 8 hours. On a 6-hour cron that is 2 Slack API calls every 6 hours — 8 calls per day — just in case there are messages.
  2. No acknowledgement back to Felix. He posts a URL or topic and gets nothing back. He has no way to know if Scout read it, used it, or failed on it.
  3. The 8-hour lookback window creates boundary ambiguity. A message posted 7h 55min before a run is included; one posted 8h 05min before is silently missed. Posts near the boundary between runs can be double-processed or dropped.
  4. Slack is being used as a database. That is not what Slack is for. Slack is a messaging system — it does not guarantee message retention, has rate limits on history calls, and its 90-day free-tier message history means older inputs eventually disappear.
  5. Sequential URL fetching blocks the entire run. If Felix posts 3 URLs and the second one takes 10 seconds to resolve, the RSS fetch is delayed by that full 10 seconds.
Felix — asks for architectural rethink
Don't just build on this one. What would you do differently instead of patching this one?
Claude Code — proposed full architectural redesign

The root problem is "treating Slack as a database." The right fix is to invert the data flow direction.

Instead of Scout pulling from Slack on a timer, Slack pushes to an endpoint the moment Felix posts. The message is stored in Supabase where Scout can read it reliably. Scout replies to Felix's message thread after the post publishes.

Proposed architecture

OLD:
Felix posts to #scout-editor
       ↓ (up to 6 hours later)
Scout polls conversations.history → reads messages → no acknowledgement

NEW:
Felix posts to #scout-editor
       ↓ (< 1 second — Slack push)
POST /api/slack/editorial  (aitrends.ng webhook)
       ↓
editorial_queue table in Supabase  (status: pending)
       ↓
felix.js reads pending rows from DB  (at Scout run time)
       ↓
Scout consumes inputs, marks rows consumed
       ↓ (after Phase 2 publishes)
complete.js calls Slack chat.postMessage with thread_ts
       ↓
Felix gets "✅ Used in: [title]" reply in his original thread

What changes

  • felix.js — 126 lines → ~30 lines. No Slack API calls. Reads from Supabase editorial_queue table.
  • New: aitrends.ng/app/api/slack/editorial/route.ts — Slack Events API webhook. Validates signing secret, saves row to DB.
  • New: supabase/add-editorial-queue.sql — table with slack_ts (unique), urls[], notes, status, used_in_post, posted_at.
  • New: replyToFelix() in slack.js — threads a reply using chat.postMessage with thread_ts.
  • New: 4 memory functions — getEditorialQueue, consumeEditorialRows, getPendingEditorialReplies, markEditorialReplied.
  • scout.js — calls consumeEditorialRows(rowIds, digest.title) after savePendingPost succeeds.
  • complete.js — after notifySlack(), calls reply chain for any consumed editorial rows.

What does not change

felix.js still returns exactly { topics, sources } — plus a new rowIds field. The rest of the pipeline (scout.js, gemini.js) is untouched. URL content is still fetched at Scout run time.

One-time Slack setup required

  • Enable Events API on the Slack app → set Request URL to https://aitrends-ng.vercel.app/api/slack/editorial
  • Subscribe to message.channels bot event
  • Copy Signing Secret → Vercel env var SLACK_SIGNING_SECRET

File 1 — NEW: aitrends.ng/supabase/add-editorial-queue.sql

-- editorial_queue table
-- Felix posts to #scout-editor in Slack → Slack Events API → /api/slack/editorial → here.
-- Scout reads pending rows instead of polling the Slack API every run.
--
-- Lifecycle:  pending → consumed (Scout used it) → posted_at set (Slack reply sent)
-- If Scout runs but no post is queued, rows stay pending and carry over to the next run.

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS editorial_queue (
  id            bigint generated always as identity primary key,
  slack_ts      text unique not null,    -- Slack message timestamp — used as thread_ts when replying
  slack_channel text not null,           -- Slack channel ID — needed to target the reply
  text          text,                    -- stripped plain-text content of Felix's message
  urls          text[],                  -- URLs extracted from the message
  notes         text,                    -- any non-URL editorial annotation Felix included
  status        text default 'pending',  -- pending | consumed
  used_in_post  text,                    -- title of the post this input contributed to
  posted_at     timestamptz,             -- set after the Slack reply thread has been sent
  consumed_at   timestamptz,
  created_at    timestamptz default now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_editorial_queue_status
  ON editorial_queue (status, created_at DESC);

ALTER TABLE editorial_queue ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY;

CREATE POLICY "service role full access"
  ON editorial_queue
  FOR ALL
  TO service_role
  USING (true)
  WITH CHECK (true);

File 2 — NEW: aitrends.ng/app/api/slack/editorial/route.ts

Directory created first: mkdir -p aitrends.ng/app/api/slack/editorial

// app/api/slack/editorial/route.ts
//
// Receives Slack Events API webhooks from #scout-editor.
// When Felix posts a message to #scout-editor, Slack calls this endpoint.
//
// This replaces the old polling approach where Scout queried conversations.history
// on every run. Now: Felix writes → Slack pushes → row saved → Scout reads from DB.

import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'
import { createClient } from '@supabase/supabase-js'
import crypto from 'crypto'

function extractUrls(text: string): string[] {
  const slackWrapped = /<(https?:\/\/[^|>\s]+)[^>]*>/g
  const urls: string[] = []
  let m: RegExpExecArray | null
  while ((m = slackWrapped.exec(text)) !== null) urls.push(m[1])
  const stripped = text.replace(/<[^>]+>/g, ' ')
  const bare = /https?:\/\/[^\s<>"']+/g
  while ((m = bare.exec(stripped)) !== null) urls.push(m[0].replace(/[.,;!?]$/, ''))
  return [...new Set(urls)]
}

function stripSlackFormatting(text: string): string {
  return text
    .replace(/<https?:\/\/[^|>]*\|([^>]+)>/g, '$1')
    .replace(/<[^>]+>/g, '')
    .replace(/&amp;/g, '&').replace(/&lt;/g, '<').replace(/&gt;/g, '>')
    .trim()
}

function verifySlackSignature(
  signingSecret: string, signature: string, timestamp: string, body: string
): boolean {
  if (Math.abs(Date.now() / 1000 - parseInt(timestamp, 10)) > 300) return false
  const baseString = `v0:${timestamp}:${body}`
  const expected = 'v0=' + crypto.createHmac('sha256', signingSecret).update(baseString).digest('hex')
  try { return crypto.timingSafeEqual(Buffer.from(expected), Buffer.from(signature)) }
  catch { return false }
}

export async function POST(req: NextRequest) {
  const rawBody = await req.text()
  let body: Record<string, unknown>
  try { body = JSON.parse(rawBody) }
  catch { return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid JSON' }, { status: 400 }) }

  // Slack sends a one-time challenge when the Request URL is first saved
  if (body.type === 'url_verification') {
    return NextResponse.json({ challenge: body.challenge })
  }

  // Validate signature on all other requests
  const signingSecret = process.env.SLACK_SIGNING_SECRET
  if (!signingSecret) {
    console.error('[editorial] SLACK_SIGNING_SECRET not configured')
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Configuration error' }, { status: 500 })
  }

  const signature = req.headers.get('x-slack-signature') ?? ''
  const timestamp  = req.headers.get('x-slack-request-timestamp') ?? ''
  if (!verifySlackSignature(signingSecret, signature, timestamp, rawBody)) {
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid signature' }, { status: 401 })
  }

  // Slack retries if we don't respond within 3s — just acknowledge retries
  if (req.headers.get('x-slack-retry-num')) {
    return NextResponse.json({ ok: true })
  }

  const event = body.event as Record<string, unknown> | undefined
  if (!event || event.type !== 'message') return NextResponse.json({ ok: true })
  if (event.bot_id || event.subtype) return NextResponse.json({ ok: true })

  const rawText   = (event.text as string) || ''
  const urls      = extractUrls(rawText)
  const plainText = stripSlackFormatting(rawText).replace(/https?:\/\/\S+/g, '').trim()
  if (!plainText && urls.length === 0) return NextResponse.json({ ok: true })

  const supabase = createClient(
    process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL!,
    process.env.SUPABASE_SECRET_KEY!
  )

  const { error } = await supabase.from('editorial_queue').insert({
    slack_ts:      event.ts as string,
    slack_channel: event.channel as string,
    text:          plainText || null,
    urls:          urls.length > 0 ? urls : null,
    notes:         plainText || null,
    status:        'pending',
  })

  if (error) {
    if (error.code === '23505') return NextResponse.json({ ok: true }) // duplicate ts
    console.error('[editorial] DB insert error:', error.message)
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'DB error' }, { status: 500 })
  }

  console.log(`[editorial] Queued: ${urls.length} URL(s), note: "${plainText.slice(0, 60)}"`)
  return NextResponse.json({ ok: true })
}

File 3 — MODIFIED: scout-agent/memory.js — 4 new functions inserted before the deduplication section

// ── editorial_queue — Slack editorial input queue ─────────────────────────────

export async function getEditorialQueue() {
  const { data, error } = await supabase
    .from('editorial_queue')
    .select('id, slack_ts, slack_channel, text, urls, notes')
    .eq('status', 'pending')
    .order('created_at', { ascending: true })
  if (error) { console.error('memory.getEditorialQueue error:', error.message); return [] }
  return data || []
}

export async function consumeEditorialRows(ids, postTitle) {
  if (!ids || ids.length === 0) return
  const { error } = await supabase
    .from('editorial_queue')
    .update({ status: 'consumed', used_in_post: postTitle, consumed_at: new Date().toISOString() })
    .in('id', ids)
    .eq('status', 'pending')  // only update pending rows — idempotent, first writer wins
  if (error) console.error('memory.consumeEditorialRows error:', error.message)
  else console.log(`  📬 Marked ${ids.length} editorial input(s) as consumed for: "${postTitle.slice(0,55)}"`)
}

export async function getPendingEditorialReplies(postTitle) {
  const { data, error } = await supabase
    .from('editorial_queue')
    .select('id, slack_ts, slack_channel')
    .eq('status', 'consumed')
    .eq('used_in_post', postTitle)
    .is('posted_at', null)
  if (error) { console.error('memory.getPendingEditorialReplies error:', error.message); return [] }
  return data || []
}

export async function markEditorialReplied(ids) {
  if (!ids || ids.length === 0) return
  const { error } = await supabase
    .from('editorial_queue')
    .update({ posted_at: new Date().toISOString() })
    .in('id', ids)
  if (error) console.error('memory.markEditorialReplied error:', error.message)
}

File 4 — REWRITTEN: scout-agent/felix.js

Before: 126 lines polling Slack API (conversations.list + conversations.history, 8-hour lookback, sequential URL fetching, no acknowledgement).

After: 60 lines reading from Supabase editorial_queue table. Key change: returns { topics, sources, rowIds } — the rowIds field lets scout.js mark rows consumed after a successful queue.

// felix.js (complete rewrite — 60 lines)
//
// OLD design: polled Slack conversations.history every run (8-hour lookback window)
// NEW design: reads from the editorial_queue Supabase table
//   Felix posts → Slack Events API → aitrends.ng /api/slack/editorial → DB row → here
//
// Returns { topics, sources, rowIds }

import { fetchContent } from './fetcher.js'
import { getEditorialQueue } from './memory.js'

export async function fetchFelixInputs() {
  try {
    const rows = await getEditorialQueue()

    if (rows.length === 0) {
      console.log('  No pending editorial inputs in queue')
      return { topics: [], sources: [], rowIds: [] }
    }

    console.log(`  Found ${rows.length} pending editorial input(s) in queue`)

    const topics  = []
    const sources = []
    const rowIds  = rows.map(r => r.id)

    for (const row of rows) {
      const urls      = row.urls || []
      const plainText = (row.notes || row.text || '').trim()

      if (urls.length > 0) {
        for (const url of urls) {
          console.log(`    Extracting content: ${url.slice(0, 70)}`)
          const content = await fetchContent(url)
          if (content) {
            sources.push({ url, note: plainText || null, content })
            console.log(`    ✅ Content extracted (${content.length} chars)`)
          } else {
            if (plainText) topics.push({ text: plainText })
            console.log(`    ⚠️  Could not extract content — using note as topic signal`)
          }
        }
      } else if (plainText) {
        topics.push({ text: plainText })
        console.log(`    Topic signal: "${plainText.slice(0, 60)}"`)
      }
    }

    console.log(`  Editorial inputs: ${sources.length} source(s), ${topics.length} topic(s)`)
    return { topics, sources, rowIds }

  } catch (err) {
    console.error(`  Felix inputs error: ${err.message}`)
    return { topics: [], sources: [], rowIds: [] }
  }
}

File 5 — MODIFIED: scout-agent/slack.js — replyToFelix() added

Read the full existing file first (72 lines), then appended after the closing brace of notifySlack().

export async function replyToFelix(slackTs, slackChannel, postTitle, postUrl) {
  if (!process.env.SLACK_BOT_TOKEN) return

  const res = await fetch('https://slack.com/api/chat.postMessage', {
    method: 'POST',
    headers: {
      Authorization:  `Bearer ${process.env.SLACK_BOT_TOKEN}`,
      'Content-Type': 'application/json',
    },
    body: JSON.stringify({
      channel:   slackChannel,
      thread_ts: slackTs,
      text:      `✅ Used in: *${postTitle}*
${postUrl}`,
    })
  })

  const data = await res.json()
  if (!data.ok) console.error(`Slack thread reply failed: ${data.error}`)
  else console.log(`  💬 Replied to Felix in Slack thread`)
}

Felix — asked to clarify setup step 1
Explain that number 1.
Claude Code — explained Supabase SQL editor step

Step 1 ("Run supabase/add-editorial-queue.sql in the Supabase SQL editor") means: open the Supabase dashboard, paste the SQL file's contents into the built-in query tool, and execute it. That is how you create the new editorial_queue table in the database.

  1. Go to supabase.com → sign in → open the tixagzzcaeqdohuyrngl project
  2. In the left sidebar, click SQL Editor
  3. Click New query
  4. Open aitrends.ng/supabase/add-editorial-queue.sql in your code editor, copy all text
  5. Paste into Supabase SQL Editor
  6. Click Run (or Ctrl+Enter)
  7. Success message appears — no rows affected is normal for CREATE TABLE

The file creates the editorial_queue table, an index, and the row-level security policy that lets Scout's service role key read and write to it. Without this, the webhook endpoint would crash with "relation does not exist" on the first message from Felix.

This is the same process used previously to run add-source-reputation.sql in Session #9.

Felix — asked to clarify setup step 2
Explain step 2
Claude Code — explained Slack Events API setup step by step

Step 2 is configuring the Slack app to push messages to the new webhook instead of waiting for Scout to pull them.

  1. Go to api.slack.com/apps and sign in with the Slack account that owns the workspace
  2. Click the app whose SLACK_BOT_TOKEN is already in scout-agent/.env
  3. In the left sidebar of the app settings page, click Event Subscriptions
  4. Toggle Enable Events to ON
  5. A Request URL field appears — paste in: https://aitrends-ng.vercel.app/api/slack/editorial
  6. Slack immediately sends a POST with a url_verification challenge. The endpoint handles this automatically and responds with the challenge string. Slack shows a green Verified checkmark within a second. If it shows an error, Vercel hasn't deployed yet — deploy first, then return.
  7. Scroll to Subscribe to bot events → click Add Bot User Event → search and select message.channels
  8. Click Save Changes

After this, every message Felix sends to any public channel the bot is a member of fires a POST to the webhook. Since the bot is already in #scout-editor, messages start arriving immediately.

[Screenshot: GitHub Personal Access Tokens → Fine-grained tokens → aitrends-cron-trigger] — Repository access: FAIT-Blog/scout-agent — Repository permissions: Read access to metadata + Read and Write access to actions — Created: Fri Jun 5 2026 | Expires: Sun Jul 5 2026 What do I do next?
Claude Code — instructed Felix to regenerate token and add to Vercel + cron-job.org

This token (aitrends-cron-trigger) is exactly right — FAIT-Blog/scout-agent with Read and Write access to Actions. No need to create a new one.

The token value was only shown once when created, so regenerate to get a usable value:

  1. Click Regenerate token → copy the new value immediately (will not be shown again)
  2. Go to Vercel → aitrends-ng project → Settings → Environment Variables → add: Key: GITHUB_PAT, Value: the token just copied
  3. Update cron-job.org with the new token value — regenerating invalidates the old one, and cron-job.org uses this same PAT to dispatch Phase 2 every 30 minutes. Skipping this step stops Phase 2.
  4. Redeploy Vercel (Deployments → three-dot menu on latest → Redeploy)

After the redeploy, posting to #scout-editor fires Phase 1 within seconds.

Felix — asked what to update at cron-job.org
What to do at Cron-job
Claude Code — explained cron-job.org Authorization header update

In cron-job.org, the PAT is sent as a header in the HTTP request that triggers GitHub Actions. It must be updated in both cron jobs (Phase 1 and Phase 2).

For each job:

  1. Go to cron-job.org → Cron Jobs → click on the job
  2. Scroll to the Headers section
  3. Find the header named Authorization
  4. Its current value is Bearer ghp_oldtokenvalue... — replace everything after Bearer with the new token
  5. Save

Do this for both the Phase 1 job (every 6 hours → dispatches scout.yml) and the Phase 2 job (every 30 minutes → dispatches complete.yml). Same new token value in both.
