Session #27 — 25 June 2026

Project: scout-agent · Focus: Gemini daily-quota cooldown — stop cron jobs wasting resources on a known-dead quota

Turn 1 — Felix's question, in full

Felix: "Have you considered that since Gemini daily quota may queue some of the cron jobs, especially in the this recent case where you have used up the daily quota (20) to correct or cleanup, could it be that when some job line up it will not have negative impact because their failure to go through/ execute will be counted as errors and the several retrials will be repeated and since it will take a long while before Gemini daily quota refreshes, there will be so many failed job attempt. So what is in place to inform the scout/cronjob to wait till there is Gemini quota thereby preventing unnessary waste of resources and accumulation of error report? Let me know if you understand me."

Restated back to confirm understanding before investigating: (1) when quota is exhausted, does the pipeline fail gracefully or repeat errors against a dead quota all day; (2) does any retry layer keep hammering Gemini pointlessly while quota is still zero; (3) is there anything that detects "quota's gone" and tells the pipeline to stand down rather than accumulate failed runs and error noise.

Turn 2 — Read the real error-handling code rather than guess

grep -n "try\|catch\|generateDigest\|generateBlendedDigest" scout.js
# confirmed each category wrapped in its own try/catch, logs and `continue`s on failure
# does NOT call markSeen() on failure — articles retried fresh next run

grep -n "gemini\|generateDigest\|generateBlended" complete.js
# (no matches — Phase 2/publishing never calls Gemini at all)

cat .github/workflows/scout.yml
# "Notify Slack on failure" step is `if: failure()` — only fires if the
# GHA job itself exits non-zero

Findings reported back: Gemini calls don't retry-storm on 429 in production code (only 503 triggers the fallback+retry loop) — that risk was specific to my own one-off cleanup scripts, not the live pipeline. The real problems: (1) RSS fetch, full-text extraction, and Tavily search all happen before the Gemini call in scout.js — so the expensive upstream work runs every category, every 6h, for zero output, while quota is dead; (2) each category's try/catch swallows the error and never re-throws, so runScout() exits 0 (success) even when every category failed — meaning the GHA "Notify Slack on failure" step never fires, so the failure is completely silent, not just noisy; (3) no quota-state tracking exists anywhere to let a future run skip early; (4) Phase 2 (publishing) is entirely unaffected, confirmed by the empty grep.

Turn 3 — Felix: "Let's talk through first"

Discussed before writing any code. Led with a concrete discovery: the model fallback only triggers on 503, never 429 — meaning gemini-2.5-flash's separate daily quota bucket had never actually been touched by any of the prior cleanup work, despite all of it hitting 429 on gemini-3.5-flash. That's a near-free fix on its own.

Laid out three further design choices with a recommendation on each: reactive detection (catch the real 429) over proactive self-counting (scout-agent's own counter can't see manual one-off work hitting the same Google-side quota, so it would give false confidence regardless); skip the entire run on a known cooldown rather than a partial skip, trading a rare missed short-lived RSS item for fully eliminating the wasted Tavily/fetch calls; alert once per day on first detection rather than on every 6-hourly skipped run. Also flagged that a normal day's legitimate usage (4 Phase 1 runs × up to 4 categories, plus editorial items, plus the daily podcast run) could already sit close to the 20-call ceiling even with zero manual work — framing this as a recurring operational concern, not a one-off artifact of cleanup days.

Turn 4 — Felix decides

Felix: "Let's go with Reactive. I have also created the Google Alert and Google Search Console for aitrends.ng." (the second sentence logged separately under Session #26's to-do confirmations)

Two design choices still open were asked directly rather than assumed: full-run skip vs. partial skip, and whether to extend the 429 fallback regardless of the cooldown system.

Felix's answers: "Skip the whole run (recommended)" / "Yes, do it now regardless of the cooldown system."

Turn 5 — Found gemini-podcast.js had its own independent copy of the same logic

grep -n "GEMINI_PRIMARY\|GEMINI_FALLBACK\|MAX_ATTEMPTS\|callGemini" gemini-podcast.js scout-podcast.js
gemini-podcast.js:23: const GEMINI_PRIMARY  = '...gemini-3.5-flash:generateContent'
gemini-podcast.js:24: const GEMINI_FALLBACK = '...gemini-2.5-flash:generateContent'
# identical signature, identical retry shape — same Google project, same
# model names, same shared quota bucket as scout.js

This meant the fix needed to land in three files' worth of retry logic (generateDigest, generateBlendedDigest, generateEditorialDigest in gemini.js, plus the separate copy in gemini-podcast.js) unless consolidated — chose to extract one shared helper rather than quadruple the new cooldown-detection logic.

Turn 6 — Built it

memory.js — added isGeminiQuotaCooledDown() / setGeminiQuotaCooldown(), single-row Supabase state matching the existing homepage_monitor pattern exactly. A cooldown from a previous calendar day is treated as stale — rather than compute Google's exact reset time (their error body's retryDelay field is a short backoff hint, not the real daily reset), the next day's first attempt is just allowed to try again, cheap to be wrong in that direction.

slack.js — added notifyQuotaExhausted(), same webhook-based pattern as notifyMonitorAlert(), fires only on a new cooldown event.

gemini.js — extracted callGeminiWithFallback(payload, label), exported so gemini-podcast.js could reuse it. Falls back to gemini-2.5-flash on either 503 or 429 now (previously 503 only). Only when both primary and fallback return 429 in the same attempt does it call setGeminiQuotaCooldown(), conditionally fire the Slack alert (only if this is a new cooldown event today), and throw a distinguishable GEMINI_QUOTA_EXHAUSTED error. Replaced all three duplicated retry blocks (generateDigest, generateBlendedDigest, generateEditorialDigest) with calls to the shared helper.

gemini-podcast.js — removed its entire independent copy (GEMINI_PRIMARY/FALLBACK constants, callGemini, the full retry loop) and replaced with an import of the shared helper from gemini.js.

scout.js — added the cooldown pre-check at the very top of runScout(), before any RSS/Tavily/Gemini work, returning immediately with one clean log line if already cooled down today. Added a check in both the Step 0.5 editorial-item catch and the main category-loop catch: on GEMINI_QUOTA_EXHAUSTED specifically, break out of the loop immediately rather than continue-ing to the next item/category, since the quota is global — the next attempt would just fail the same way.

scout-podcast.js — same pre-check at the top. For the mid-run break: first wrote return totalQueued inside the nested per-video catch block, then caught it immediately on review — a bare return would skip the function's own trailing "✅ Podcast Scout complete" summary log. Fixed by introducing a quotaExhausted flag, checked at the top of the outer channel loop, set and break-ed from the inner video loop — preserves the final summary log even when cut short.

Session #28 — 13 July 2026

scout-agent · Gemini quota cooldown timezone bug

Felix — diagnosis request
Scout has published zero posts since July 7th. Gemini's free tier quota resets daily. Leading theory: the quota-exhausted cooldown flag in Supabase is stuck "on" and never resetting, rather than the pipeline genuinely hitting a fresh quota wall every single day.
Claude Code — investigation

Finding 1 — GHA Workflows Are Running

Scout cron runs 4×/day (00:00, 06:00, 12:00, 18:00 UTC). Podcast runs 1×/day (06:00 UTC). Homepage-monitor runs 4×/day. All enabled. Recent run logs show conclusion: "success" on every run — no failures. But success = skip (cooldown active) + process.exit(0), not success = posts published.

Finding 2 — Every Gemini Call Site Shares One Cooldown

Four functions hit Gemini: generateDigest(), generateBlendedDigest(), generateEditorialDigest() in gemini.js, and gemini-podcast.js. All route through callGeminiWithFallback() (Session #27 refactor), which calls setGeminiQuotaCooldown() when both models429 in the same call. Both scout.js and scout-podcast.js call isGeminiQuotaCooledDown() before any work. One cooldown, one table, shared across all pipelines. Verified in Supabase: hit_at: "2026-07-13T01:52:03.792+00:00".

Finding 3 — The Retry Logic Doesn't Cause a Storm

MAX_ATTEMPTS = 3, 12 s delays. Tries gemini-3.5-flash first, then gemini-2.5-flash. Each call is a Google API call, so worst case is 6 API calls per logical digest on 503 retries. The 0 */6 * * * cron prevents storms — one logical attempt per 6 hours. The real issue is not over-retry but under-detection: the cooldown skips the entire run cleanly, so the system exits 0 and never alerts.

Finding 4 — Total Daily Call Budget

4 RSS runs/day × ~4 categories + podcast + editorial = ~18–21 calls on a happy path. Gemini free tier: 20 requests/day per model. That means the pipeline genuinely runs out of quota every single day on the happy path — the quota exhaustion itself is not a bug. The bug is that the cooldown flag, once set, never clears.

Finding 5 — The Cooldown Timezone Bug

The cooldown check at memory.js:357-368 compares UTC calendar dates:

const hitDate = new Date(data.hit_at).toISOString().slice(0, 10)  // "2026-07-13"
const today = new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10)               // "2026-07-13"
return hitDate === today

Both sides use UTC dates. Gemini's quota resets at midnight Pacific Time (= 07:00 UTC in summer). The ~01:47 UTC GHA cron run (= 6:47 PM PT) always passes the cooldown check (new UTC day), tries Gemini (still exhausted — still previous PT day), hits429, and re-sets the cooldown with the new UTC date. This blocks the 05:00 UTC run (= midnight PT, when the quota actually resets) and every subsequent run that UTC day. The cooldown was self-perpetuating: each day's first run to pass the check would re-set it before midnight PT, blocking the fresh-quota window permanently.

Traced through GHA run logs day by day: July 7 05:00 UTC (= midnight PT) was the last successful run (queued "Alibaba Restricts Anthropic Tools"). By 09:23 UTC (= 2:23 AM PT) quota was exhausted. Every run from July 8 onward hit the same pattern: 01:47 UTC re-set the cooldown, 05:00 UTC and all subsequent runs skipped. The Supabase row confirmed: hit_at = "2026-07-13T01:52:03".

Fix — Elapsed-Time Staleness

Replaced the UTC-date comparison with a time-elapsed check:

const STALE_MS = 20 * 60 * 60 * 1000  // 20 hours

const elapsed = Date.now() - new Date(data.hit_at).getTime()
return elapsed < STALE_MS

20-hour threshold is timezone-agnostic. Covers the worst-case gap: quota exhausted at 4 AM PT, resets at midnight PT next day = ~20 hours. If more than 20 hours have passed, the quota has definitely reset. No calendar-date math, no PT-to-UTC conversion, no daylight-saving edge cases.

node --check memory.js passes clean. Diff is 10 lines changed, self-contained to one function.

Deployment plan (not yet executed)

  1. Commit and push the memory.js fix
  2. After fix is live: DELETE FROM gemini_quota_cooldown WHERE id = 1; to clear the stuck row
  3. Trigger manual workflow_dispatch on scout.yml
  4. Confirm in logs it actually runs Gemini calls (not the 17-second skip)
  5. Monitor next few scheduled runs to confirm cooldown clears daily on its own
Session #28 Summary

Root cause:

UTC-vs-PT timezone mismatch in the cooldown staleness check. The cooldown compared UTC calendar dates, but Gemini's quota resets at midnight PT. The ~01:47 UTC run re-set the cooldown before midnight PT, permanently blocking every run for the day.

What was fixed:

  • memory.js — isGeminiQuotaCooledDown() now uses elapsed-time staleness (20-hour threshold) instead of UTC calendar-date comparison

What was NOT changed:

  • RSS cron schedule (remains 4×/day, 0 */6 * * *)
  • Podcast cron schedule (remains 1×/day, 0 6 * * *)
  • cron-job.org triggers (remains as-is)
  • setGeminiQuotaCooldown() — no change, still upserts current UTC timestamp
  • All other pipeline logic unchanged

  • gemini-3.1-flash-lite — 200, working
  • gemini-2.0-flash — 429 (quota exhausted)
  • gemini-2.0-flash-lite — 429 (quota exhausted)
  • gemini-2.5-flash — 404 (deprecated)

Code changes

gemini.js rewritten:

  • Two Google model constants → one GEMINI_URL (3.5-flash) + one GROQ_URL
  • callGemini() simplified (no URL parameter — uses module-level constant)
  • New callGroq() — translates Gemini's contents format to OpenAI messages format
  • New normaliseGroqResponse() — wraps Groq output in Gemini response shape (candidates[0].content.parts[0].text)
  • callGeminiWithFallback() — tries Gemini, retries on 503 (3 attempts, 12s delay), falls back to Groq on non-retryable errors, cooldown on 429
  • No caller changes needed — generateDigest, blended, editorial, podcast all use the same interface

memory.js — comment updated to reflect single-model quota tracking.

.env — GEMINI_API_KEY swapped to new key, GROQ_API_KEY added.

Anthropic and tools skipped (0 AI-signal articles). Phase 2 published the TikTok post at 05:30 UTC. Pipeline is alive again after 8 days of silence.

Known limitation

gemini-3.5-flash on a fresh free-tier key will hit the same 28-day billing cliff that killed the old key. When that happens, the fix is the same: create another new project, generate a new key, swap in .env + GH Secret. The Groq fallback provides a safety net during any transition gap.
